time:
2011-09-25T18:28:55Z
class:
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/decider/SameShardAllocationDecider.java
comments:
use index iteration over iterator
How come you made this change? What's the improvement?

I'll make those changes on other places as well, but, doing some perf tests over large number of shards shows hotspots when using iterator (the foreach statement).

Interesting! I always assumed the compiler would make both these versions the same (the enhanced/new for loop being only a syntactic sugar). Also, I've often heard/read that in most cases using an `Iterator` would be beneficial. But I decided to look into it some more, and I understand your collection is most likely implementing [`RandomAccess`](http://download.oracle.com/javase/6/docs/api/java/util/RandomAccess.html) in which case an index iteration is faster.

All in all, as your perf tests show this to be superior in your case, it's all good! :) Thanks for your feedback!

Yea, one would hope that this will be the case, but as I also found out, index based access is faster, especially in these areas that are hotspots when it comes to shard allocation logic.

time:
2011-09-25T18:01:39Z
class:
comments:
Reformatted and amended the example configuration file

Edited elasticsearch.yml:

* Separated different sections (using headers)
* Added more information about nodes configuration
* Added more information about various index configurations and their effects
* Added information about setting network and HTTP configuration
* Reworded information on gateway, recovery, discovery

The example configuration file should allow operations stuff to quickly
get a sense of ElasticSearch features relevant for systems support,
and to understand how to configure node, cluster, network and discovery settings.

The aim here is to vaguely respect the most often changed configuration settings,
while having some top-to-bottom conceptual integrity.

Table of Contents:

* Cluster
* Node
* Index
* Paths
* Memory
* Network And HTTP
* Gateway
* Recovery Throttling
* Discovery
